Airplane Inspects Situation in Northern Shandong 73

Dispatch from Jinan: The situation in northern Shandong recently has been the focus of attention from all sides. Shi Bangfan, deputy captain of the Second Aviation Team, flew north the day before yesterday to inspect along the railway line as far as Tianjin. He returned to Jinan safely after five hours. According to him, from north of Jinan to north of Pingyuan, only a small number of Jin army cavalry were seen moving back and forth. North of the Yellow River Cliff station, the Jin army had defensive works, but the number of people was very small. There was only one trainload of soldiers and one armored train in Dezhou, with no more than two battalions of people. From north of Dezhou, although there were defensive works in the Sangyuan, Zhuanhe, and Cangzhou areas, there were very few troops. In summary, there were less than one brigade of Jin army south of Cangzhou. North of Cangzhou, near Machang, along the embankment of the Hai River and the Grand Canal, the Jin army had built extremely strong defensive works, seemingly to defend against the south and the northeast. There were two trainloads of soldiers at Tianjin East Station. Overall, there were very few Jin troops along the road, and they immediately lay down in the trenches when they saw the airplane, showing extreme panic and no preparation for a southern attack. (April 10)

Situation of the Japanese Mine Warfare Fleet Arriving in Hankou 74

Dispatch from Hankou: The First Mine Warfare Flotilla of Japan, consisting of fifteen destroyers, led by Rear Admiral Goto, commander of the Japanese Navy, aboard the flagship Naka, arrived in Hankou one after another at 12:00 noon on the 9th, and were berthed in the Japanese Concession on the river. The fleet, in addition to the flagship Naka, commanded by Goto, was divided into four squadrons. The first squadron consisted of four ships: the Kuretake, Wakatake, Sanae, and Sawarabi. The second squadron consisted of four ships: the Tsuta, Ogi, Susuki, and Fuji. The third squadron consisted of four ships: the Fuyou, Asagao, Bungei, and Karukaya. The fourth squadron consisted of three ships: the Hishi, Ashi, and Kawa. Each destroyer had one lieutenant commander, one ensign, one engineer ensign, one engineer, one mechanic, and a number of sailors, totaling more than 1,420 officers and sailors on all ships. When the fleet arrived in Hankou, it fired salutes to the Chinese Navy, and the Chinese warships stationed in Hankou returned the salutes to show their welcome. Japanese consuls and merchants were waiting on the riverbank, and all Japanese stores were flying flags. After the fleet arrived in Hankou, Commander Goto, accompanied by Lieutenant Akiyama Teruo of the Sawarabi, Lieutenant Itakura Tokushi of the Wakatake, Lieutenant Tachibana Masao of the Sanae, Lieutenant Yoshikawa Keizou of the Kuretake, Lieutenant Katsumitsu Take of the Tsuta, Lieutenant Hayashi Kamono Suke of the Susuki, Lieutenant Kibayashi Masafuku of the Ogi, Lieutenant Shima Sou Toshio of the Fuji, Lieutenant Awata Tadayoshi of the Fuyou, Lieutenant Arajima Tsutaeru of the Asagao, Lieutenant Gasai Kouaku of the Bungei, Lieutenant Watari Reiji Na of the Karukaya, Lieutenant Akenabe Yuuji of the Hishi, Lieutenant Isaki Shunji of the Ashi, and Lieutenant Neda Gennojo of the Kawa, and guided by Tanaka, the Japanese consul stationed in Hankou, visited Director He Chengjun of the Commander-in-Chief's headquarters at 2:30 p.m., and spoke for about ten minutes. They then visited Mayor Liu Wendao of the Hankou Special Municipal Government, and then visited the private residence of Xia Douyin, commander of the Wuhan Garrison in the Japanese Concession, before returning to their ships. At 4:00 p.m., He Chengjun, Liu Wendao, and Xia Douyin boarded the flagship Naka to return the visit, talked for about ten minutes, and then went ashore. In the evening, at 7:00 p.m., He, Liu, and Xia held a banquet in the Great Hall of the Municipal Government, to entertain Rear Admiral Goto, the lieutenant commanders of each ship, the Japanese consul stationed in Hankou, and the naval commander stationed in Hankou, totaling more than 20 people. Those accompanying the Chinese side included the heads of various departments and committees of the provincial government, the heads of various bureaus and councilors of the municipal government, the commanders of various armies, divisions, and brigades stationed in Hankou, and the naval commander, totaling more than 40 people. He Chengjun, as the chairman, gave a welcome speech, saying (Today, your fleet has come to Wuhan to visit various people in Hankou, and we are very grateful. China and Japan are of the same race and the same culture, and their relationship in history is very friendly and close. This time, Rear Admiral Goto has come to China for sightseeing, and has come to Wuhan on the way. He will soon return to his country. The people of Wuhan hope that Rear Admiral Goto will make further progress in promoting Sino-Japanese friendship and further consolidate Sino-Japanese diplomatic relations after returning to his country. On behalf of the people of Wuhan, I would like to toast you and wish you good health), and so on. After the speech, Goto gave a reply. The banquet ended at 9:00 p.m. It is said that Goto has scheduled a banquet on the flagship Naka for Director He and others on the evening of the 10th, and will lead the fleet eastward to Wusong on the 11th. (April 9)

Qingdao British American Tobacco Company Labor Strike Escalates 75

Dispatch from Qingdao: The British American Tobacco Company in this port, citing the presence of troublemakers among the workers, unilaterally suspended work last month, leaving more than 2,000 workers unemployed. The party and government authorities, concerned that too many unemployed workers would affect Qingdao's security, tasked the municipal government with negotiating with the manager of the British American Tobacco Company, requesting that it resume work as soon as possible. The company immediately put forward conditions such as stopping the labor movement and dismissing bad workers. The municipal government has accommodated them separately. As a result, both sides agreed to resume work on April 4. However, the workers, on the grounds that their living standards had increased in recent years but their wages had not, demanded that the company slightly increase their wages to maintain their livelihood. However, the company only agreed to take two dimes from each box of cigarettes to distribute to the workers, averaging less than one cent per worker. As a result, the workers were very dissatisfied and uniformly refused to resume work on that day, and petitioned the municipal government. The municipal government, believing that the workers were close to blackmail and were obviously being exploited by reactionary elements, immediately ordered the Public Security Bureau to arrest all nine of their representatives when the workers gathered for a meeting, and they were detained in the Public Security Bureau. On the 9th, the workers again planned to gather a crowd to petition the municipal government to release the arrested representatives. The Public Security Bureau received the news and sent a team to stop them. As a result, a conflict broke out between the workers and the police, injuring dozens of workers and arresting approximately 30 people. (April 9)

Two Major Projects on the Yellow River in Shandong 76

Plugging the Breach at Hutantan Repairing the Spring Embankment

Dispatch from Jinan: This year, there are two major important projects on the Yellow River in this province: (1) plugging the breach at Hujiatan in Lijin; (2) the spring embankment project for the entire river. The former has already been estimated by the River Affairs Bureau to cost 119,000 yuan to plug the breach, while the latter has been requested by the River Affairs Bureau to cost 460,000 yuan. Although the projects are urgent, the Finance Department must wait for the approval of the River Affairs Bureau's higher-level agency before it can issue the funds. Therefore, as of now, not a single penny has been issued. The counties downstream of Lijin believe that if the breach at Hujiatan is not plugged as soon as possible, then the peach blossom flood will rise in an instant, making construction impossible. The people of several counties will suffer from fish floods. Therefore, they sent representatives to Jinan to appeal to the provincial government, the Finance Department, and the River Works Committee. At the last meeting of the provincial government committee, it was resolved to order the River Works Committee to review and issue the funds. This afternoon, the River Works Committee held its fifth regular meeting and resolved: (1) The 119,000 yuan for plugging the breach at Hujiatan will be sent to the provincial government to order the Finance Department to allocate the funds as soon as possible so that construction can begin. (2) The 460,000 yuan for the spring embankment requested by the River Affairs Bureau will first be submitted to the provincial government to order the Finance Department to allocate 190,000 yuan for materials within the budget in three installments: 80,000 yuan in the first installment, 60,000 yuan in the second installment, and 50,000 yuan in the third installment, so that materials can be purchased. The remaining 260,000 yuan will be submitted to the provincial government to order the Finance Department to allocate the funds after this committee sends personnel to survey and estimate. The disaster-stricken representatives from Lijin and other counties were all overjoyed to hear that plugging the breach at Hujiatan was scheduled and that the funds for the spring embankment were available, but it is not known whether the Finance Department will be able to allocate the funds as scheduled. (April 9)

Shandong Finance Department Returns Military Expenses Requested by Sun Liangcheng 77

Dispatch from Jinan: Since the establishment of the Shandong Provincial Government in Tai'an, the military expenses requisitioned by former Chairman Sun Liangcheng in various counties amounted to a huge sum of more than 8 million yuan. After the provincial government moved to Jinan, the Finance Department believed that the military expenses requisitioned were all local public funds, and immediately ordered Li Hui, the chief of the Second Section of the department, to appoint specialists to actively sort out the matter. It took several months to complete the task. Subsequently, it was submitted to the provincial political conference for consideration of ways to repay the funds. The provincial government then issued the matter to the Economic and Financial Reorganization Committee for careful review and formulation of repayment standards, which were divided into three categories: (1) For those requisitioned by the provincial government and the Finance Department with printed receipts, it will be classified as the first category and will be repaid in installments over three years starting from the 19th year. (2) For the formal army units and supply stations that requisitioned funds with printed receipts, it will be repaid in installments over three years starting from the fourth year after the first category of funds has been approved for repayment. If there are no funds in the first category, it will be repaid in installments starting from the 19th year. (3) For the miscellaneous army that requisitioned funds freely and was supplied by the local government, and for the self-defense corps of the people that requisitioned funds, without orders from the provincial government and the department, it will be classified as the third category and will be cleared and repaid through special surcharges by the local government starting from the 19th year. This method has been reported to the provincial government and submitted to the conference for resolution, ordering the department to comply. Upon receiving this, the Finance Department immediately notified various counties, and printed four types of military expense repayment vouchers. Every day at 4:00 p.m., the department chief, Yuan Jiapu, convened the heads of the first, second, and third sections and the personnel in charge of the treasury in the office to review and fill out the vouchers. (Note: These military expense repayment vouchers are designated for offsetting local land tax and grain tax, and have the same effect as payment notices.) The department chief ordered the vouchers to be handed over to the finance bureaus of the respective counties for safekeeping, and they will be submitted for offsetting at the expiration date. Military expenses requisitioned from the miscellaneous tax items of various counties may be submitted for offsetting at any time. Yesterday (the 4th), for the new Second Brigade's military expenses advanced by Zouping County, which belonged to the treasury funds, totaling 90,661.94 yuan, 12 vouchers were issued in accordance with the first and second categories' method of repaying in installments over six years. The handling of military expense cases requisitioned by other counties is still under discussion. (April 9)

Completion of the Chang-Heng Highway in Hunan Province 78

He Jian Personally Attends the Ceremony and Visits Mount Heng, Changsha Correspondence: Mount Heng, Hengshan, is one of China's famous Five Sacred Mountains. The mountain is located in Hengshan County, Hunan. The Changsha to Hengzhou highway has now been completed. Liu Yuehou, the director of the Provincial Highway Bureau, specifically submitted a request to the Provincial Government for approval to hold the opening ceremony in Hengzhou on April 10th. He Jian, the chairman of the Provincial Government, invited all members of the Provincial Government, all members of the Provincial Party Department, consuls of various countries stationed in Hunan, the president of the High Court, and others to go to Hengzhou to attend the opening ceremony and visit Mount Heng. It is planned that they will depart from Changsha by car at 7:00 AM on the 10th and arrive in Hengzhou at 1:00 PM. The opening ceremony will be held in Hengzhou at 2:00 PM. At 6:00 AM on the 11th, they will travel by car from Hengzhou to Hengshan to visit Mount Heng, and will stay overnight in Hengshan that evening. At 6:00 AM on the 12th, they will return to the province by car from Hengshan, arriving in Changsha around 12:00 PM. All matters concerning meals and accommodation in Hengzhou will be the responsibility of the Highway Bureau. Su Yongqing, a section chief from the Fourth Route Headquarters, and Adjutant Wang Fu have been dispatched to Hengshan by steamer on the 9th to arrange all matters concerning meals and accommodation on Mount Heng. The Highway Bureau has prepared five cars for transportation. After He Jian leaves the province, the affairs of the Fourth Route Headquarters will be handled by Chief of Staff Guo Chiping. The affairs of the Anti-Banditry Headquarters will be handled by Chief of Staff Liu Qingchu, and the affairs of the 15th Division Headquarters will be handled by Chief of Staff Liu Yinggu. The duties of the Provincial Government will be handled by Secretary-General Yi Shuzhu, who will issue orders and then depart. (9th)

Abnormal Movements of Yan Zhongru's Troops in Baoqing 79

Changsha Correspondence: The troops of Yan Zhongru, the commander of the Independent 5th Brigade, were originally reorganized from the 156th Brigade of Wu Shang's former 52nd Division. Last year, a small part of Wang Pei's brigade of the Wu Division mutinied in Changde, and the name of the 52nd Division was abolished. The Yan Brigade was reorganized into the Training Brigade of the Newly Organized 8th Division. Unexpectedly, Zhou Lan's troops of the New 8th Division mutinied again in Baoqing and were led into Guangxi by Tang Shengming. The Yan Brigade then had no affiliation and was approved by He Jian to the General Headquarters to be reorganized into the Independent 5th Brigade, still under the control of He Jian. The Yan Brigade consisted of two regiments. The first regiment commander was Li Xuan, and the second regiment commander was Wan Fangzhi. Both had already been transferred from western Hunan to Baoqing for training. Recently, due to the rampant banditry in Jiangxi and the emergency situation in Pingxiang and Liuyang, He Jian ordered the entire Yan Brigade to move to Changsha and Xiangtan, intending to send them to Liuyang to suppress the bandits. Yan Zhongru himself moved from Baoqing to Changsha last week, and the headquarters was set up outside Xiaowumen at the Military Officer Training Institute. The Second Regiment, Wan Fangzhi, has also complied with the order and arrived in the Yijiawan area of Xiangtan to await orders. The First Regiment, Li Xuan, was originally scheduled to arrive in Changsha from Baoqing on the 8th, and the provincial capital had prepared accommodation. Unexpectedly, on the 7th, Li's regiment had an incident in Baoqing. First, they cut the telegraph lines, cutting off traffic between Baoqing and Changsha. The Chang-Bao bus service also stopped on the 8th. As for the actions of Li's regiment, because the telegraph lines were down and transportation was cut off, the provincial authorities have not yet received accurate reports. However, Tian Jifeng, the magistrate of Xiangxiang County, sent a telegram early on the 8th, saying that the troops in Baoqing had mutinied and that Li's army sentries had been posted to Wenzishan, which belongs to Yongfeng in Xiangxiang County, to guard against the provincial army. He Jian was very surprised to receive the report. In addition to sending personnel to investigate the truth for processing, he has also ordered Yan Zhongru to go to Xiangtan and Xiangxiang to handle matters as appropriate. (April 9)

Narrowing Down of Subsidiary Businesses of the Eastern Railway 80

A Committee Has Been Established to Conduct Reviews

Printing House and Publishing Department to Be Abolished

Harbin Communication, 6th: Regarding the case of using both Chinese and Russian languages passed by the Eastern Railway Board of Directors on the 25th of last month, the Board of Directors recently ordered the Railway Bureau to organize a committee to study implementation methods. It is heard that in the future, when implemented, the translation departments of various offices under the Railway Bureau will be removed and a separate compilation or translation office will be established. All documents promulgated by the Railway Bureau will be translated by this office, and the official documents submitted by the stations along the line to the Bureau will also be translated by it and then distributed. This method can not only supervise the abuse of power by Russian Bureau chiefs on our side, but also unify the official document format on the Bureau side. Regarding the Railway Bureau's reduction of subsidiary businesses, a committee has also been established by the Railway Bureau to begin reviewing. The scope of the reduction is approximately: (1) Pine Oil Manufacturing Plant, (2) Climate Sanatorium, (3) Restaurant, (4) Hotel, (5) Travel Agency, (6) Agricultural Experiment Field, (7) Milk Plant, (8) Milk Manufacturing Plant, (9) Cheese Manufacturing Plant, (10) Unimportant Business Agency, (11) Printing House, (12) Publishing Department, (13) Sawmill, (14) Sleeper Impregnation Plant, (15) Soda Factory. Among them, the business agency is particularly focused on by the Chinese side for reduction, because the business agency established by the Eastern Railway in major ports in Shanghai and Tianjin is not sufficient to offset expenditures in terms of income, and there is no need for such long-distance transportation in terms of transportation. In order to prevent the Russian side from using false pretenses to promote communism, at a minimum, it has also been decided to strive to reduce staff and streamline administration. As for the vehicles detained by the Ukrainian Railway, even after being handed over once, they are still not dispatched. The reason given is that during the time of Old Russia, 2,700 vehicles were detained by the Eastern Railway, and the Eastern Railway vehicles detained now can just offset this. The Chinese Director of the Eastern Railway believes that it concerns the property of the Qing Railway, so he urges the Railway Bureau to continue negotiations. Before Mo Dehui goes to Russia, it is planned to resolve all road cases related to affairs. It has also been decided to convene a board meeting next Wednesday (i.e., the 9th), with a total of eight agenda items, mostly for purchasing materials, houses, and construction projects. In terms of nature, they should be easily passed.

Jiangsu Provincial Government Distributes Saigon Rice 81

The First Batch Is Distributed to Twenty Counties Including Jiangning

Each County Receives a Maximum of 105,000 Catties

The Jiangsu Provincial Government previously received a letter from Committee Member Lu of the Food Regulation Committee regarding the purchase of Saigon rice (specifically to relieve the food shortage panic in various counties), which is about to arrive in Zhenjiang. He requested that various measures be planned in advance. After the 281st Provincial Committee meeting, it was decided that Committee Member He Yushu should liaise with the Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce to handle the distribution of rice. Now, after repeated consultations between He and the Chamber of Commerce, a distribution plan has been drafted and approved by the Provincial Government's 283rd meeting yesterday. The plan is as follows:

Distribution Area: According to the autumn survey report of the Civil Affairs, Finance, and Agriculture Committee last year, the following nineteen counties with more than 30% disaster severity are designated as the distribution area for this batch of rice: Jiangning, Jiangpu, Liuhe, Xinghua, Dongtai, Baoying, Gaoyou, Zhenjiang, Danyang, Liyang, Funing, Yancheng, Kunshan, Lianshui, Tongshan, Fengxian, Xiaoxian, Suining, and Ganyu. However, the Department of Agriculture and Mines previously purchased a large batch of rice seeds in Taixian and transported them to Yancheng, Funing, Xinghua, and Baoying for lending. At that time, it was stated that when this batch of Saigon rice arrived, it would be appropriately returned for relief. Therefore, although the disaster situation in these counties is below 30%, they are still included in the distribution area to fulfill the previous agreement.

Distribution Quantity: The Saigon rice purchased this time totals 1,500 tons. The Provincial Government will order the Department of Agriculture and Mines to telegraph the county governments of Jiangning and the other twenty counties, consult with the chambers of commerce of each county, consider the needs, and send personnel to Zhenjiang to pick up the rice with funds before April 20th. However, each county shall not exceed 105,000 catties.

Rice Price: The price of this batch of Saigon rice, including transportation costs, is approximately 15.5 yuan per 150 catties. Compared to the current market price, each bag is approximately two yuan cheaper. The government's purchase of foreign rice is originally intended to regulate the people's food supply, and it does not seem necessary to strictly comply with the market price, let alone make money from it. Therefore, the price will be fixed at 15.5 yuan per 150 catties and distributed to the counties. The counties will then add the cost of water and deduct the actual amount for distribution and sale to poor households to benefit the poor.

Fierce Battle Between Police and Bandits in Yangcheng Lake 82

Six Kidnapped Victims from Zhangyan Town Rescued

Suzhou Correspondence: The gangs of Zhang Zhaohua and Taibao Ashu from Yangcheng Lake, after being defeated by the anti-bandit army, navy, police in Shengjiabang of Fenghu and Da Yao of Chefang this month, the Zhang Zhaohua gang from Haizhou sneaked back to Yangcheng Lake on the 9th. After the anti-bandit army found out, they secretly reported to the General Command. Commander Hu then ordered the troops and Director Gong of the Third District of the Water Police to supervise the patrol boats of the Eleventh, Twelfth, and Thirteenth Squadrons of the Water Police to arrive at the beach along Yangcheng Lake by the morning of the 11th to encircle the bandit boats of the Zhang Zhaohua gang and cooperate in suppressing them. Yesterday morning (11th) at about 6:00 AM, Xu Boying, the captain of the Eleventh Squadron of the Water Police, personally led his squadron of fourteen patrol boats to Louzitou near Weijingtang Town on the shore of Yangcheng Lake and anchored. He immediately sent out detectives to scout for bandit tracks. He learned that the Zhang gang had a total of twenty-two bandit boats with more than 300 bandits. The boats were hiding more than 20 kidnapped victims from Zhangyan Town, Jinshan. They sailed to Yangcheng Lake on the 10th and arrived at Taiping Bridge on the morning of the 11th. Captain Xu received the report and led his squadron to Taiping Bridge. Unexpectedly, when they arrived at Taiping Bridge, the bandits had turned to Weijingtang. Captain Xu had no choice but to return to Weijingtang. At that time, it was about 1:00 PM. Captain Xu also learned from scouts that the bandits were staying in Louzitou. Captain Xu then ordered the first, second, and third squads to encircle and advance in three routes. At about 3:00 PM, they finally encircled the bandit boats. The bandits, seeing the arrival of the government troops and running out of ammunition, tried to find a way out but could not. Zhang Zhaohua then ordered the bandits to open fire and resist arrest. Captain Xu also ordered his squadron to counterattack and opened fire for four hours until about 7:00 PM when it ceased. The bandits, seeing the situation was not good, fled for their lives. In this battle, Captain Xu shot down three bandit boats, seized four rifles, and rescued six kidnapped victims, male and female, from Zhangyan Town, as well as a boatman and his wife. This morning (12th), he led the team back to Suzhou to report to the district headquarters. Director Gong immediately interrogated the kidnapped victims one by one. It was learned that the female victim, Zhang Xiumei, was 29 years old and from Zhangyan Town. She was kidnapped by the Haizhou gang when they looted the town on the 1st of this month. Her father's name is Zhang Qifeng, who runs the Zhang Jisheng Pharmacy, and her brother's name is Xuenian, who is a doctor. When the bandits looted the town, Xiumei's parents were not at home, only her brother and sister were in the store. It was heard that when the bandits looted, she and her brother hid on the roof of a neighbor's house, but were seen by the bandits, who threatened them with guns and kidnapped Zhang Xiumei and her brother together and put them on a boat. Then they robbed a small steamer and sailed to Guanwang Temple to distribute the spoils. On the 5th, Zhang Xuenian was released first and ordered to go back and prepare 10,000 yuan to redeem his sister at the Yangcheng Lake. The next day (6th), the bandits burned incense at Guanwang Temple and were repelled by the anti-bandit army at about 6:00 PM. The bandits then fled with the kidnapped victims. The other five kidnapped victims, (1) Huang Gongshou, 11 years old, (2) Huang Quqing, 14 years old, (3) Huang Wenjun, 13 years old, (4) Yao Shuping, 14 years old, (5) Yao Jiping, 13 years old, are all from Zhangyan and were kidnapped from the Second Primary School in Jinshan County. The boatmen Chen Abing and his wife Ru were shot and injured by the bandits at the time. After Director Gong's questioning, he sent personnel to the Tiancizhuang Bo Xi Hospital to treat the injured boatmen Chen Abing and his wife. The other six kidnapped victims were ordered to be escorted by Inspector Ma Lumei to the General Command to request instructions. Commander Hu, after confirming that they were indeed kidnapped victims, appointed Inspector Hong of the Sixth Branch of the Yan District to send Zhang Xiumei and the other six to a hotel to live in and notified their families to come to Suzhou to pick them up. It is heard that the bandit gangs of Zhang Zhaohua and Taibao Ashu have fled to Yuanjiahuling in Qingpu New Town and Yangsanta Temple in Yangcheng Lake.

Another Correspondence: Xu Boying, the captain of the Eleventh Squadron of the Third District of the Water Police, was ordered by Director Gong the night before to lead his squadron's first squad leader Yu Hongxun, second squad leader Wang Qi, third squad leader Gu Dingkui with fourteen boats to depart from Suzhou to Yangcheng Village (this village is a small island in the middle of Yangcheng Lake, surrounded by water, with an area of about ten square li) to search, but found no trace of bandits. So they returned to Weijingtang. When the boats were traveling, they hired many civilian boats to sail in front, and the gunboats were hidden behind the civilian boats to avoid the target of the bandits. At 2:30 PM yesterday (11th), it was learned that the bandits were in Louzitou (this place is two li south of Taiping Bridge and five or six li north of Weijingtang), with twenty-two boats and about 300 bandits. It was a merger of the Mao Zilong and Zhang Zhaohua gangs from Haizhou. They then drummed the boats forward, and after seeing the bandit tracks, they landed and dispersed at a distance of 1,500 meters, ordering the second squad leader Wang Qi to take charge of the right wing, the third squad Gu Dingkui to take charge of the left wing, and Captain Xu himself led the squadron leader Yu to take charge of the middle road to bombard the bandits. The bandits also landed and attacked. The bandits were all wearing black short clothes and had four mobile machine guns, more than forty Mauser pistols, and more than one hundred rifles. During the fierce battle, the bandit leader blew the horn to direct the battle. The water police also blew the horn, because the water police had four bugles, they blew them all together, using the sound of the bugles to create chaos. From 3:00 PM, the fierce battle continued until 8:00 PM, killing five or sixty bandits. The bandits then collapsed and fled towards Yangyi Lake. The water police then bravely pursued. The road was muddy after the rain, and the policemen fell and got up. They crossed three river surfaces and chased for five or six li. As a result, they seized three bandit boats, four firearms, and rescued six kidnapped victims. On the water police side, squadron leader Yu fell and coughed up blood. Zhang Maosheng, a policeman from the second patrol boat of the first squadron (18 years old, from Lili), was shot in the lower jaw and had three front teeth knocked out (now sent to the Gospel Hospital). About six or seventy water police were on the front line in this battle. The rescued kidnapped victims were (1) Huang Wenjun (13 years old, style name Shuping, lives at the junction of Zhangyan and Hengpu), (2) Huang Gongshou (11 years old, style name Lianfang, brother of Wenjun), (3) Huang Quqing (14 years old, brother of Gongshou), (4) Yao Shuping (14 years old, lives in Yaojiawan, Zhangyan, father's name is Hongfei), (5) Yao Jiping (13 years old, brother of Shuping), the above five are all boarders at the Second Higher Primary School in Jinshan County, (6) Zhang Xiumei (29 years old, lives east of the Zhangyan Town Banqiao, father's name is Zhang Qifeng, 66 years old, mother's name is Pan, 62 years old, brother's name is Yaonian, 40 years old, one older sister and one younger sister, both married, I am unmarried because there are few people in my family.)

According to Zhang Xiumei, on the third day of the third lunar month (April 1st), when a large gang of lake bandits looted Zhangyan, there were more than thirty boats. Four bandits went to her house to rob and kidnapped her and her brother together. They disembarked north of the river. The bandit boat where her brother and sister were staying was larger and had five bandits. Among the five bandits, there were three bandit leaders, one named Boss Yan, one named Boss Cao, and one was called Old Old Man by the crowd, but his name was unknown. Initially, after the bandits distributed the spoils at Guanwang Temple, they sailed to a temple. After arriving there, the bandits drove all the kidnapped victims ashore, and the bandit leader Zhang Zhaohua interrogated them one by one. The bandit leader was about forty years old, wearing a small hat and a camel-hair robe, with small blisters on his face and a fierce appearance. Seeing that the kidnapped victims at this time were all men, women, old, and young, some women were holding babies, and some couples were crying together, it was extremely miserable. The bandit leader was very strict during the interrogation and took notes while asking questions to determine the ransom price. The amount of the price depended on how much family property each person answered. In addition to the students being kidnapped from the Jinshan Second High School, there were also the principal Wang Chenchu and teachers Zhang (sports), Lin Mingjian, and Zhou Gengxin. Now one person, Lin Zhou, has escaped danger, but Principal Wang and Teacher Zhang are still trapped by the bandits. When the bandit leader asked a partner from a certain bowl shop, because he replied that he had no money, he was shot and killed and his body was abandoned in the lake. Then the bandits ordered her brother Yaonian to go back to negotiate and send letters to the families to prepare the ransom tickets. She wanted to go back with him, but the bandit leader did not allow it. So she asked her brother to consult with the bandit leader Boss Yan about what to do if there was any indecency. She was allowed to be responsible for protection, and Yaonian also negotiated with the bandit to move the five students Huang Wenjun and others from Ergao to her boat to accompany her. These five students are very innocent and cheerful, and the bandits all call them (Five Gods of Wealth). After her brother returned on the 5th, the bandits once tricked the five students Huang Wenjun and others to leave the boat to commit indecency, but the bandit shouted and stopped them. Fortunately, they were not insulted. When she was kidnapped and disembarked, she was wearing leather clothes because it was cold. She remembered that on one of the hottest days, the bandits ordered the female victims on other boats to go ashore for a walk and changed the clothes they had robbed for them, but she did not receive this preferential treatment. She also said that the bandit boat was sailing day and night, never stopping. The bandit leader had a password to transmit to each boat every day. The bandits on her boat did not know how to read much, so the five students Huang Wenjun and others read it for them. It roughly consisted of (love), (compatriot), (agreement), (peace), (consensus) and other words, written in pencil. From the 6th, they fought with the government troops four times. The first time was the most intense, and the firing lasted for two and a half hours. The old old man on her boat was shot and killed by the government troops, and the body was dragged back by the bandits, placed at the bow of the boat, and abandoned at night. Later, there were two more fights. When the fire was opened, the five young students Huang and others were lying beside her. When the bandits were robbing, they wrapped red and green cloth strips around their arms as a sign. Usually, they used passwords. This time, the water police opened fire, and bullets were flying everywhere. Her boat was also hit by many bullets. It is expected that the two boats seized by the other water police also had kidnapped victims, but they had already escaped. Zhang, a manager of a pawnshop in Zhangyan, was beaten the worst among the kidnapped victims.

Now the Eleventh Squadron has returned to the city today, and the seized firearms, boats, and kidnapped victims have been sent to the district headquarters. Among the four firearms seized, two have the Lushui imprint. Also, the boatmen Chen Abing and Chen Ru were rescued at the same time, and their feet have been shot by bandit bullets.

In the southeast area of ​​Yunzi Mountain in Yangcheng Lake, the military and police opened fire with bandits from 9:00 AM today, stopping for about an hour. They made contact again from 2:00 PM, and had not stopped as of 6:00 PM. The sound of rifles and machine guns was heard very clearly at the Waitangkou Station. The location seemed to be in the Maota area, seven miles away from Waitangkou Station.

After receiving the provincial order, the county government has instructed the defense groups of each township and their subordinates to comply with the report.

Convening a Pingdiao Meeting Recently, rice prices have continued to increase, and the poor people who eat grains are sighing about their hardship. Therefore, the county government scheduled to convene a meeting of various districts and groups in the city at the afternoon of the fourteenth of this month to discuss solutions.

Suzhou 83

The Egg Boat Was Intercepted by Lake Bandits. Zhenxin Egg Row outside the Banmen entrusted the boatman Zhou Genbao to Wu Changfeng Row in Chenfang Bridge Town, Qingpu, to load 92,500 duck eggs. When returning to Suzhou, they passed through Da Yao Village in Chefang District and were intercepted by a large gang of lake bandits. The bandits kidnapped the boat owner Zhou Genbao and his daughter Da Yuan, and the boatman Zhou Ajin and Xu Jinlong to the bandit boat. When the troops arrived to pursue them, the two sides opened fire and the bandits retreated to the north. Zhou Genbao was unfortunately hit by a stray bullet in the waist and died, abandoning his body in the river. Zhou Dayuan begged the bandits bitterly before being released. However, the two boatmen are still in the hands of the bandits. As for the egg boat, it has been rocked back to Suzhou City by another boatman yesterday, but there are only a few thousand eggs left in it.

The Arrest of Suspected Accomplice of Bandits. The Taihu Bandit Suppression General Command reported that Chen Ziheng, a Henan native, was hiding in Wujiang and was suspected of being an accomplice of bandits. Please arrest him immediately. He was secretly ordered to the Wujiang county magistrate, who sent the police to arrest Chen in the afternoon of yesterday (12th) and escorted him to Suzhou to the General Command. After being interrogated by the military law office, he claimed to be a native of Luoshan, Henan, 51 years old, and denied being an accomplice of bandits. He was immediately detained.

Wuxi 84

The Municipal Preparatory Office Is Preparing to Close. The Wuxi Municipal Preparatory Office was previously resolved to be reorganized at a meeting of the Provincial Government. It was scheduled to be closed at the end of March. Later, it received an order from the Department to postpone it and maintain it as it was. The Provincial Government transferred the case to the Department of Civil Affairs and Construction to review and reply on the measures after the conclusion of the Wuxi Municipal Office. The two departments have now discussed the measures and reported them to the Provincial Government. It was proposed for discussion at the Provincial Government meeting on the 11th and decided to abolish the Wuxi Municipal Preparatory Office immediately to comply with the new Provincial Government's intention to save government expenses and promote practicality. As for the matters under the jurisdiction of the Municipal Preparatory Office, after the conclusion, it has also been decided to change them according to their nature and return them to the various bureaus under the county government and the management of the urban and rural autonomous region offices. The Municipal Preparatory Office originally had four sections: General Affairs, Finance, Public Works, and Society. It has been decided that the matters under the jurisdiction of the Finance Section will be handled by the Finance Bureau under the county government, the Public Works Section will be handled by the Construction Bureau, the sanitation matters of the Social Sanitation Section will be handled by the Public Security Bureau, the social survey matters will be handled by the Social Survey Office, and the industrial and commercial matters will also be incorporated into the Construction Bureau. As for the matters under the jurisdiction of the General Affairs Section, they will also be assigned to the county government and the First District Office according to their nature. Sun Zuji, the concurrent director of the Municipal Preparatory Office, has also instructed the various sections to rush to complete the conclusion, and to be separated and merged once the provincial order is received.

Yuanqiao Public Security Bureau Arrests Thieves. Wang Weixin, the director of the Thirteenth Sub-Bureau of the Yuanqiao Town Public Security Bureau in the Fifth Autonomous Region, was patrolling with the police at the foot of the West Jiaoshan the day before (11th) and saw six or seven people gathered together suspiciously. When he went forward to inquire, they ran away as soon as they saw the police. Two people were caught after chasing, and a bundle of sack rope and a small rattan basket were found on them, containing six fake bombs made from cigarette cans. They were immediately taken to the bureau for interrogation. According to one of them, Pu Zihong, and the other, Tang Agen, both from Huangtutang, Jiangyin, intended to rob a certain village in Jiangyin. Director Wang immediately sent them to the County Public Security Bureau for interrogation yesterday according to their confession.

The Theft of Pig Boats Was Captured. The day before yesterday, Yang Yichang Meat Zhuang in Suzhou sent a partner to a pig row in Luoshe Town, Wujin County, to buy thirty-seven large pigs and transport them back to Suzhou by boat. At 12:00 PM that night, when passing through Baitangwei, they encountered a bandit boat. Seven bandits jumped out and robbed twenty-nine large pigs. Unexpectedly, the next morning, the bandit boat sailed to the Lujiangkou of Xueqiao Bridge and attempted to sell the pigs ashore. The members of the chamber of commerce found out the flaw and arrested the bandits Chen Ziqing, Chen Shikuo, Chen Shenggu, Wang Ada Xue Amen, and Zhang Arer on the spot. They were immediately sent to the corps headquarters for interrogation. The six thieves all confessed to the robbery of the pig boat and confessed that there was still one accomplice in Wuxi. After receiving the confession, the corps sent the six arrested thieves, along with the seized large pig bandit boat, to the county government for interrogation.

Mulberry Leaf Roves Must Pay Taxes and Obtain Licenses. Chen Liangdong, the director of the county Finance Bureau, believes that most of the mulberry leaf roves in the county intend to take advantage of tricks. They do not obtain licenses and privately buy and sell mulberry leaves on behalf of customers, collect brokerage fees, and operate privately, which is inconsistent with the regulations. Yesterday, he issued a public notice to the roves, limiting them to come to the bureau to pay taxes and obtain fourth-class dental licenses within ten days to comply with the regulations and increase tax revenue. At the same time, he sent special personnel to the countryside to check. If there is a private opening without a license, or if the license is used improperly, they will be severely punished according to the regulations and will not be lenient.

Changzhou 85

Investigation into Rice Reserves: Wuyi County Rice Prices Increase Daily, Food Prospects Cause Great Panic. The previous county government meeting decided on measures to maintain food supply, resolving that the County Chamber of Commerce and the First District Office would first investigate the local food situation and then discuss maintenance measures. It is now learned that the investigation results reported by the rice industry indicate that the urban area has approximately 20,000 piculs of local rice and approximately 10,000 piculs of Saigon rice, sufficient to maintain supply for two months. Because rice merchants have limited reserves, they are currently procuring Saigon rice in Shanghai for relief purposes.

Yan Xiangfu was stabbed by the robbers, and all of his cash, clothing, and decorations were stolen. On the 11th, Township Chiefs Wu Zhigen and Zhao Xibao reported the case to the county, requesting an investigation.

Jingjiang 88

Changan City Burned and Looted by Bandits: At 3:00 AM on the 9th, a crowd of about one thousand bandits suddenly arrived at Changan City, carrying flags and surrounding it on all sides. Knowing they could not resist, the government troops retreated to Gushan. After the bandits entered the city, they first searched and looted each household, then set fires. Only three houses in the entire city remained standing. Losses are estimated at over 100,000 yuan. That same night, the Wenwudian Salt Card office was also robbed by bandits. Fortunately, the troops had prepared in advance and nothing was obtained. Only one cook was killed and one cart driver was kidnapped.

Resignation of Anti-Smuggling Brigade Commander Approved: Xu Hongjin, commander of the Tenth Anti-Smuggling Brigade, submitted a document to the Anti-Smuggling Bureau a few days ago requesting his resignation. An instruction has now been received approving the resignation. His vacancy will be filled by the commander of the Jiangyin Lu Brigade.

Jiashan 89

Suppression Troops Arrive at Yuhui: The remnants of bandit leader Taibao A-Shu's gang in Dianshan Lake, after looting Zhangyan, have been rampaging through villages in Qingpu, Songjiang, and Jiashan, committing all sorts of illegal acts, including robbery, kidnapping, arson, and murder. After being jointly encircled and suppressed by the Jiangsu Provincial Suppression Troops, they retreated to the Hongzi Dike in Yuwei. Now, they have been bravely pursued by the suppression troops, resulting in the deaths of three bandits, injuries to over ten, and the capture of four. Two bandit ships were seized. The suppression troops also suffered some losses. The captured bandits are being sent to the province for legal proceedings, and the troops are pursuing the remaining bandits relentlessly, vowing to annihilate them completely.

Russian Stealing Suspects Arrested: On the morning of the 11th, two Russians suddenly came to the Tongsheng Noodle Shop to buy goods and exchange foreign currency. The shop assistants were temporarily overwhelmed, and eleven yuan were stolen. They then went to a butcher shop outside the East Gate to buy one yuan worth of meat and presented a ten-yuan foreign note for exchange. The shop assistant, not paying attention, was also cheated out of six yuan. Fortunately, it was quickly noticed, and the Public Security Bureau was notified to send police to arrest the two Russians. Director Gu personally interrogated them. The Russians claimed to be Romanian, had passports, and denied the theft. After the shop assistants were brought in for confrontation, the Russians finally admitted and offered to compensate Tongsheng and the butcher shop for their losses.

Boatmen Violently Rape Young Maid: Hu A-Si, a boatman from the Zha Pu West Gate, was overcome with lust. He violently raped Chunfang, a young maid from the Yang family next door, causing injuries. After the maid's master noticed, she was rushed to the Chengji Hospital in Zha Pu for treatment. Knowing he had caused trouble, A-Si fled that night. The Yang family has filed a complaint with the county government, requesting that A-Si be arrested and severely punished. A-Si's mother and brother attempted to escape after receiving news of the incident, but were placed under surveillance by the Zha Pu Public Security Bureau.

Qianjiawei and Nanlu Concurrently Robbed: At midnight on the 6th, over fifty bandits suddenly arrived at Qianjiawei Town, speaking in the local dialect. They fired shots to intimidate the residents and stormed into the market. The local public security branch only had a small number of police officers who, being outnumbered, dared not resist and scattered. The bandits then looted at will, targeting over sixty shops, causing significant losses. After the looting, they shouted and left with their stolen goods. At the same time, on the evening of the 6th, Nanlu, a place about three miles north of Xincang Shantang Town, was also attacked by bandits. Twenty to thirty bandits arrived with torches and weapons. Several well-established shops in the town, such as Yaotongfeng and Lufuchang, were robbed. It was also reported that the wife of a butcher shop owner was injured on the head with a meat cleaver by the bandits for refusing to reveal where the silver was hidden. Her injuries are quite severe.

The methods for repayment of principal and interest on the bonds have also been drafted, with payments to be made in eighteen installments from this year to 1939, every February and August.

Foreign Minister Wang Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning 95

Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting arrived at the North Station at around 7:00 AM yesterday by overnight express train from Beijing and returned to his residence on Guba Road. Motives for Signing the Sino-French Commercial Treaty 96

Ministry of Foreign Affairs Received Note from French Envoy on the 9th

Telegraphed Shanghai to Retain Zhang Weihan, Temporarily Prevent Return to Yunnan

Zhendan News Agency reports: The Sino-French commercial treaty was once suspended due to the issue of new taxes in Yunnan. After Hu Shize, secretary of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, went to Beijing, he contacted the French envoy, but the French side delayed and the French envoy did not go south as scheduled and did not reply to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' telegrams. Zhang Weihan, our Yunnan negotiator attending the meeting, had also purchased a boat ticket and was preparing to return to Yunnan on the 15th of this month. However, recently, the atmosphere of Sino-French negotiations has become active again. On the 9th of this month, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs received a note from French envoy Madé, stating that he would go south soon to sign the Sino-French commercial treaty. Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting also telegraphed Shanghai to retain Zhang Weihan and suspend his return to Yunnan, waiting for the French envoy to go south. It is reported that Zhang will meet Foreign Minister Wang in Shanghai for instructions before deciding on his next steps.

Commercial Reorganization Council Requests Speedy Conclusion of Egyptian Commercial Treaty 97

The Commercial Reorganization Council submitted a document to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs yesterday, stating: "The increase in import taxes on tobacco leaves in Egypt has caused significant losses to our country due to the lack of a commercial treaty with that country, almost leading to a complete halt in exports. Please forward this request to the Ministry, requesting a speedy negotiation of a commercial treaty to save the situation." On the 8th of this month, a letter was received from the Shanghai Tobacco Leaf Association, stating: "Our country's tobacco leaves have always been exported to Egypt, with a large volume exported annually. Between 1918 and 1919, our country's exported tobacco leaves paid an import tax of 25 to 30 piastres per kilo (Egyptian currency). Later, our country's exported tobacco leaves were specially improved and exports greatly increased. Egypt's import tax also increased accordingly, from 30 piastres to 70 piastres per kilo. As a result, tobacco merchants stopped exporting, and exports gradually decreased, eventually falling to several dozen items per year. In recent years, the country has been levying 90 piastres per kilo on tobacco leaf imports, causing our country's exports to become even scarcer. This is the situation of Egypt's increased tobacco leaf import taxes, with our country's tobacco leaf exports decreasing year by year, almost coming to a complete halt in recent years. Tobacco leaves have been hit hard, with business plummeting. There are more than tens of millions of planting households in the producing areas. Maritime transportation has stopped, and livelihoods are being threatened. Tobacco merchants in Shanghai have accumulated a mountain of goods purchased in previous years, suffering huge losses. The goods have no market, and finance is stagnant, greatly affecting the tobacco leaf industry. It is also heard that the country's new regulations provide extra preferential treatment for countries with treaties. Our country does not have a commercial treaty, so there is no hope of reducing the import tax on our country's tobacco leaves, but instead it has been doubled, starting from March 17th, to 180 piastres per kilo (calculated at 17 shillings and 1 pence per piastre, totaling approximately 1.9 yuan in Shanghai currency per kilo, which is 2.25 pounds). If no rescue measures are taken quickly, our country's tobacco leaves will no longer be able to be exported to Egypt, tobacco merchants and planting households will suffer greatly, and the impact on commerce and people's livelihood will be profound and huge. In order to save past losses and plan for future development, the association hereby requests your esteemed association to forward this request to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to quickly negotiate a treaty with Egypt to reduce the import tax on tobacco leaves, etc. The tobacco merchants will be very grateful. Respectfully submitted to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs." It was noted that this matter was thoroughly stated by the former General Chamber of Commerce in 1927, detailing the different tax rates for countries with and without treaties for imported tobacco leaves, and requesting the former Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce in Beijing to forward this request to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for speedy negotiation of a commercial treaty to save the situation, and the association also elected representatives to go to the capital to petition. However, three years have passed and the commercial treaty has not been completed, and the country's tobacco leaf import tax has been further increased. Our Chinese tobacco leaves will no longer be able to be imported into that country. In desperation, the association reiterates its previous request and respectfully requests your esteemed Ministry to review and approve the previous case, quickly negotiate a commercial treaty with that country, and strive to remedy the situation. The tobacco merchants will be most grateful. Respectfully submitted to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs.

Shen Bingqian, President of the Shanghai District Court, Took Office Yesterday 99

Yang Wenjun Temporarily Serves as Chief Prosecutor

The position of President of the Shanghai District Court, left vacant after Yang Zhaosun was transferred to the Special District Court, has been filled by Shen Bingqian, the Chief Prosecutor of the Court, who has been promoted to Acting President by the Ministry of Justice. The order was received several days ago, but because Shen's position as Chief Prosecutor was still awaiting the arrival and handover of the new appointee, Liu Maochu, both were to be sworn in together. However, Liu has not yet arrived. Therefore, Shen formally took office as President of the Court yesterday morning, to be followed by a swearing-in ceremony later. At 9:00 AM, Shen held a simple seal-receiving ceremony in the first courtroom of the court. Therefore, no invitations were sent to various circles. After receiving the seal, a Yuanhao notice was issued, stating: "For the matter of the notice, it is hereby proclaimed that Shen Bingqian has been appointed Acting President of the Jiangsu Shanghai District Court by Order No. 645 of the Ministry of Justice. He assumed office on April 12, 1930, and a supplementary swearing-in ceremony will be held on another date, and the relevant reports will be submitted separately. This notice is hereby issued to inform all litigants and others under the jurisdiction of the court." Because the position of Chief Prosecutor has not yet been filled by a new appointee, President Shen has temporarily appointed Yang Wenjun, a prosecutor of the court, to act as Chief Prosecutor.

Shen Jinghua, Director of the County Public Security Bureau, Resigns 100

Unable to Meet Police Expenses

Shen Jinghua, Director of the Shanghai County Public Security Bureau, is currently unable to cope with the police expenses. Although the Jiangsu Department of Finance has provided a subsidy of 2,000 yuan, the accumulated debt is already huge, making it a drop in the bucket. The directors of various sub-bureaus have already pawned almost everything. In recent days, they have been coming to the city to demand back pay. Shen himself lacks the Midas touch and is unable to cope. Currently, the food supply for the police officers is unsustainable, and he is deeply concerned that they may be driven to desperate measures, with dire consequences. Rather than delaying the matter, it is better to resign early. Therefore, he submitted a report to the county government yesterday, requesting that someone be appointed to replace him.

Record of Contemporary Figures 101

Zhang Jingjiang took the night train to Beijing last night.

Wang Chonghui and Wei Daoming took the night train from Beijing to Shanghai last night and arrived here this morning.

Opposition to Japanese Warships Conducting Large-Scale Maneuvers in National Territory 102

After eighteen warships from the Japanese First Torpedo Squadron came to China, they freely sailed to Nanjing, Hankou, and other places along the Yangtze River. Despite unanimous opposition from various circles, the squadron not only failed to restrain themselves and retreat but will also sail from Wusong to the vicinity of Zhoushan on the 16th to conduct large-scale spring maneuvers with all the warships. This is a disregard for our national sovereignty. Upon hearing the news, various community groups and party branches in this city have protested. The Coal Industry Reorganization Committee, the Fifth District Party Headquarters, the Third District Party Headquarters, the Ninth Branch of the Third District, the Twenty-First Branch of the Second District, and the Tenth Branch of the Fifth District have all sent telegrams to express their opposition, with extremely strong language.

Facts of Japanese Exclusion of Chinese 103

Those Without 100 Yuan and With Calloused Hands Are Not Allowed to Disembark

Chinese traveling to Japan for tourism or business have been repeatedly denied disembarkation and deported back to China. Although the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has negotiated with the Japanese authorities, Japanese officials have declared that there is no such thing as excluding Chinese from traveling to Japan. However, according to Mr. Wu, a restaurant merchant who was deported from Japan, Chinese traveling to Japan, except for wealthy merchants, are welcomed to disembark. Other businessmen or workers (such as those in the kimono, restaurant, chef, barber, and other craft industries) must have their hands examined by Japanese customs officers and police detectives for callouses, and their luggage checked for at least 100 yuan in cash. Those without cash and calloused hands are not allowed to disembark.

14,000 Bags of Foreign Japonica Rice Arrive in Shanghai 107

Notes on Shipping Accidents 108

"Ningshao" Damages a Pontoon The Old Ningshao steamboat of the Ningshao Company, which arrived in Shanghai yesterday from Hankou, ran into an accident. On the afternoon of the 10th, at 5:30, when the ship arrived at Pukou, it was docking at the China Merchants Wharf in that port. At that time, the Jiangtian steamboat was also docked there in preparation for He Yingqin's trip to Hankou. The Ningshao steamboat had to change its course to the Sanbei Wharf. At this moment, the tide was strong. When the Ningshao steamboat was turning around, it had to avoid a warship and collided with the Wuxiang and Jiangtian steamboats, causing the ship's hull to crash into the pontoon bridge of the Jinpu Railway. The outer hull of the pontoon was damaged by the Ningshao. The shipowner, Eddie Gren, reported the incident upon returning to Shanghai yesterday, and the Ningshao has sent a letter to the Jinpu Railway Bureau stating that it will be responsible for the repairs if the accident is found to be the fault of the Ningshao.

British Ship Runs Aground Shanghai News The Beijing City, a ship managed by the Shanghai British trading firm Jardine Matheson & Co., Ltd., which specializes in the Shanghai-London route, has a load capacity of 6,700 tons and was built in 1920.

Page 14

This time, the ship was coming to Shanghai from Europe. It first went to Vladivostok to load groceries, then to Dalian to transport soybeans. Unexpectedly, when sailing in the Korean Sea near Geomun Island on the morning of the 10th, at 5:00 AM, there was heavy fog. The ship ran aground on a reef about fifteen nautical miles northeast of Geomun Island. The bottom of the front cabin was pierced by the reef, and seawater rushed into the ship, causing it to sink immediately. Eighty-one passengers on board gathered on the deck. The crew gave them life jackets, and they were preparing to abandon ship when the captain urgently sent out an SOS distress signal. At that time, a fishing boat from the Hayashi Gumi Company in Shimonoseki, Japan, happened to be in the area and received the alert. Spotting a flare, it came to the rescue and evacuated the eighty-one passengers and part of the crew to Geomun Island for temporary shelter. Later, the management office of the Ellerman Lines in Japan received a telegram about the Beijing City's accident and dispatched the Japanese ship Ocean Maru to the rescue, transporting the passengers and crew to Japan first. The Beijing City's hull, with cargo in each cabin, gradually sank into the sea after taking on water, and there is little hope of salvage. There were also goods from Shanghai on board. It was originally scheduled to arrive in Shanghai on May 3rd and depart for England and Germany on May 5th. Now, the local branch of the company has received a telegram and canceled the export schedule. It is reported that none of the crew or passengers were injured.

Record of Foreign Merchants Seizing Yangtze River Shipping 109

Shanghai shipping merchants are planning to salvage Yangtze River shipping, and more ships have recently resumed service. Since Chinese ships reduced their services last year, foreign merchants have seized most of the freight transport on the Yangtze River ports. It will take a lot of effort to recover this business. Shanghai shipping merchants consider the Yangtze River shipping as the most important inland route in China. If this route cannot be salvaged, Chinese ships will never have a chance to expand. A recent investigation into the business seized by foreign merchants has yielded shocking results, which are detailed below.

Loss of 80% of Freight Charges There are currently six shipping companies operating between Shanghai and Hankou, including Chinese, British, and Japanese companies. Chinese merchants own three of these companies. Although they have twenty ships, less than one-third of them have been operating during the past year. British and Japanese ships, on the other hand, have twenty-six ships that regularly travel between the two ports. On average, foreign ships can make eighteen or nineteen trips per week, while Chinese ships only make three or four trips. Chinese merchants have found that the freight charges for goods shipped from Hankou to Shanghai amount to 4 million taels per year. Last year, Chinese shipping companies only received 25% of the total annual revenue, while foreign companies such as Taikoo, Jardine Matheson, and Nisshin received 75% (3 million taels) of the freight revenue.

Cotton Transportation Dominated by Foreign Merchants The largest cargo shipped from Hankou to Shanghai is cotton. The provinces of Henan, Shaanxi, Hunan, and Hubei can produce 9 million dan of cotton per year. After deducting the cotton transported to other ports, about 1.6 million bales are shipped to Shanghai. Currently, there are six cotton mills in Hankou, including the First, Zhenhuan, Yuhua, Shenxin, and Chu'an mills, and more than thirty cotton firms, mostly operated by people from Xianning. Three of these mills pack and ship cotton to Shanghai every year, making it a major source of cargo for ships on the Yangtze River. After Chinese ships suspended their services last year, British and Japanese ships competed fiercely for cotton transportation. Last year, Taikoo Company's cotton transport volume increased sharply from 150,000 bales to 400,000 bales. Nisshin Company also increased its volume from 230,000 bales to 400,000 bales. Jardine Matheson increased its volume to 300,000 bales, and Xiangtai Lines also transported a significant amount. Chinese ships, however, only got a small fraction of the business.

Dockworkers Come to Shanghai for Assistance After the labor unrest at the Lingjiang Company in Chongqing, British and Japanese ships ignored the issue and continued to transfer ships from the upper reaches to Shanghai to operate on the Shanghai-Yichang route, refusing to accept any wage increases. After the Yichang Dockworkers' Union demanded wage increases and went on strike in April, the foreign ships in the upper reaches treated the dockworkers in the same way as they treated the Lingjiang workers. However, the workers had to work to make a living, and any work stoppage would harm their livelihood. Foreign merchants were determined not to compromise. It has been confirmed that the Yichang Dockworkers' Union has decided to send representatives from Yichang to Shanghai to seek assistance from the Shanghai General Labor Union and negotiate wage increases with the shipping companies in order to protect their livelihood and avoid being oppressed by foreign merchants.

Record of Shipping Representatives Petitioning in the Province 110

Revocation of River Management Fees

Former Director Wang of the Jiangsu Construction Department proposed in July last year to collect 5% of the revenue from both passenger and cargo tickets of inland small steamships as river management fees. He also issued collection rules and set a deadline for mandatory collection, which led to shipping merchants in various ports requesting their respective shipping associations to appeal for exemption. The Shanghai Shipping Association convened a joint meeting of various associations and stated that commercial ships were burdened with numerous taxes. They sent telegrams to the central party headquarters, the Executive Yuan, and the Ministry of Transportation, Ministry of Finance, and Ministry of Industry and Commerce, as well as the provincial party headquarters and the provincial government, requesting revocation. The Ministry of Transportation approved the request, but the provincial government replied that it had been approved through meetings and was not easy to approve. The Chairman of the Shanghai Shipping Association, Yu Qiaqing, telegraphed President Chiang Kai-shek of the National Government, requesting him to sympathize with the merchants and order the provincial government to revoke the fees. Representatives have gone to Beijing to petition the Ministry of Transportation and the Executive Yuan, but the issue has not been resolved. It is now heard that the representatives went to the province the day before yesterday, at the beginning of the reorganization of the provincial government and the beginning of the renovation of politics. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Shanghai representative Zha Hongbin, Suzhou representative He Shaotang, Wuxi representatives Zhang Jianmen and Shen Xijun, Wujin representative Shao Boan, Nanjing representative Pan Xieting, and Zhenjiang representative Tao Shoubai went to the provincial government to petition. Secretary-General Jin of the provincial government met with them and was well aware of the shipping merchants' suffering. He promised to forward their intention to the chairman for review. At 2:00 PM in the afternoon, they went to the Construction Department to petition. Director Sun met with them personally. The representatives described the various burdens of the shipping merchants in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, as well as the decline in business and the bandit situation. Director Sun was aware of the difficulties of the shipping merchants and adopted the representatives' opinions, stating that this case was not easy to establish, because it had gone through many procedures and would have to wait for a few weeks of investigation before a solution could be found. The representatives were satisfied and bid farewell.

Another Surge in Chinese Silk Exports to the US 114

Due to Expected Increase in Import Tariffs by the US Government

Recently, there has been a surge in Chinese silk exports to the United States. Two company ships exported more than 4,000 bales of raw silk, worth about 5 million yuan, in the past two days. A large number of shipments to the United States are expected in the next few days. This is because there are rumors that the US government will increase import tariffs on Chinese silk starting next month. Therefore, Chinese silk merchants are taking advantage of this opportunity to export as much as possible. However, if the US government actually implements the increase in import tariffs, the sales of Chinese silk in the US will be greatly affected in the future.

Ministry of Industry and Commerce Investigates Living Conditions of Workers in the City 115

The Ministry of Industry and Commerce has sent Chen Bingquan to Shanghai to investigate the living conditions of workers and industrial production in the city. It has sent a letter to the Municipal Government requesting assistance. Rope Makers' Salary Increase Movement 116

The wages of the employees hired by the rope makers are calculated on a monthly basis. In recent years, due to the rising cost of living, the wages earned by the employees have not been enough to cover their expenses. They have been requesting wage increases from their respective shops. Since last year, the shop owners have made some wage increases. Now, the employees of the shops that have not made any wage increases are making requests to their shop owners and informing them of the wage increases made by other shops. The shop owners are not pleased and have suspended more than ten employees. The employees discussed the matter and decided that the wages in their industry are too low, with the highest wages being only ten yuan per month. In the face of rising prices, they should be increased. They must seek uniform implementation, starting with an investigation of the wage levels in each shop and increasing them according to the highest wage. After the investigation is completed, they will hold another meeting to discuss the amount of the increase.
